The Five Negative Attributes: Meaning and Nuance
Al-Bajuri defines each negative attribute and clarifies the rationale for the term 'negative'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why five divine attributes are called 'negative' (salbiyyah) and how their meaning as negations affirms positive qualities in Allah.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are positive affirmations about God expressed through negating their opposites.

Al-Bajuri now clarifies a subtle point about the five attributes that follow existence: they are termed 'negative' (salbiyyah). This does not mean they are absent in God; rather, each attribute is understood as the negation of a deficiency. For example, 'pre-eternity' negates having a beginning. This passage explains each one and cautions against misunderstanding the label 'negative.'

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Notice the five attributes listed and the phrase 'salb kaza' for each.
The passage ends with 'fatadabbar' – a call to reflect.
2
Identify the five attributes and their negations
For each of the five attributes, find the specific negation mentioned. Write them down: qidam negates priority, baqa' negates posteriority, etc.
These are the core definitions of the attributes in this context.
3
Understand the key nuance
Al-Bajuri explicitly says the attributes are 'thabitah' (affirmed) for Allah, not 'maslubah' (negated). The negation is in the interpretation, not the reality.
This guards against thinking negative attributes imply imperfection.
4
Reflect on the phrase 'fata dabbar'
Consider why the author urges contemplation. What is the deeper benefit of understanding this distinction?
It clarifies God's perfection and prevents anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبيَّةٌ إنما نُسِبَتْ للسلب؛ لأنها مُفَسَّرَةٌ به؛ إذ القِدَمُ: سَلْبُ أوَّليَّة الوجود، والبقاءُ سَلْبُ آخِرِيَّةِ الوجود، والمخالفة للحوادث: سَلْبُ المماثلة لها، والقيام بالنفس سَلْبُ الافتقار والوحدانية: سَلْبُ التعدد. وعُلِمَ من ذلك أن المراد بكونها سلبيةً أن معناها سَلْبُ كذا لا أنها مَسْلُوبَةٌ عن المولى ؛ إذ هي ثابتة له لا مسلوبة عنه. فتدبر.
His saying: 'And the five after it are negative (salbiyyah).' They are only attributed to negation because they are interpreted by it: for pre-eternity (qidam) is negation of priority of existence, perpetuity (baqa') is negation of posteriority of existence, dissimilarity to contingents (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) is negation of similarity to them, self-subsistence (qiyam bi al-nafs) is negation of need, and unity (wahdaniyyah) is negation of multiplicity. And it is known from that that what is meant by their being negative is that their meaning is negation of such-and-such, not that they are negated of the Lord; for they are affirmed for Him, not negated of Him. So contemplate.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage explains why the five attributes following existence (i.e., pre-eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingents, self-subsistence, and unity) are called 'negative' (salbiyyah). The reason is that each is interpreted (mufassarah) as a negation of its opposite. Specifically: pre-eternity negates having a beginning; perpetuity negates having an end; dissimilarity negates resembling creatures; self-subsistence negates needing a place or supporter; unity negates multiplicity. The key nuance is that calling them 'negative' refers to their meaning being a negation of something, not that the attribute itself is negated from God. On the contrary, these attributes are positively affirmed (thabitah) for Allah. The passage thus guards against the misunderstanding that 'negative attribute' implies absence in God. The author ends with 'so contemplate' (fatadabbar), urging careful reflection on this distinction.

Key Terms
السلبية
القدم
البقاء
المخالفة للحوادث
القيام بالنفس
الوحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'negative attribute' means the attribute is not present in God, or that it is a deficiency.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the negation is in the meaning (e.g., qidam means 'no beginning'), but the attribute itself is positively affirmed of God (thabitah lahu).

Checkpoint
What does 'negative attribute' (sifah salbiyyah) mean according to this passage?
A) The attribute is itself negated of God
B) The attribute is not real, only linguistic
C) The attribute is interpreted as a negation of its opposite
D) The attribute is shared by God and creatures

Key Takeaway
Negative attributes are positive affirmations about God expressed through negating their opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's attribute of 'self-subsistence' (qiyam bi al-nafs), do you feel a deep trust that He needs nothing from you, yet He is fully aware of your every need? How can you turn that into a source of reliance on Him alone starting today?
?
Consider the attribute of 'dissimilarity to contingents' (mukhalafat). Is there any image or mental picture of God you still hold that resembles His creation? What concrete step will you take to purify your conception of Allah from such similarities?
?
If 'unity' (wahdaniyyah) means negation of multiplicity, then what 'multiplicities' in your life—like fears, desires, or loyalties—compete with your devotion to Allah? What will you do today to remove at least one of those rivals from your heart?

The Meaning of 'Thumma' in the Attributes of Allah
Al-Bajuri explains the role of 'thumma' and the order of negative before positive attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'thumma' in the transition from negative to positive attributes of Allah indicates order of mention (al-tartib al-dhikri), not temporal sequence, and why the order of negation before affirmation is justified by the analogy of purification (takhliyah) before adornment (tahliyah).

Core Idea
'Thumma' signals order of exposition, not time: purification before adornment.

In this passage, al-Bajuri addresses a subtle point about the word 'thumma' (then) used by Sanusi when moving from the attributes of negation to the attributes of meanings. Some might mistakenly think this implies a temporal delay. Al-Bajuri clarifies that 'thumma' is purely for order of mention, justified by the analogy of cleansing before dressing. This lesson unpacks his explanation and the underlying logic.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
Consider why the word 'thumma' could be problematic if interpreted as temporal sequence in God's attributes. The passage states that such a delay would imply originated attributes, which is impossible.
2
Recognize the solution
Al-Bajuri explains that 'thumma' indicates order of mention (al-tartib al-dhikri), not temporal order. This means the author simply chose to mention the negative attributes before the positive ones.
3
Appreciate the analogy
The order of negation before affirmation is likened to purification (takhliyah) before adornment (tahliyah). Just as one cleans himself before putting on fine clothes, the removal of imperfections is prior to the affirmation of perfections.
4
Note the refutation of the Mu'tazila
The repetition of the word 'yajibu' (it is necessary) is explained as a refutation of the Mu'tazila who deny the necessity of the attributes of meanings. This shows the polemical context.
5
Consider the gloss by al-Ajhuri
Al-Ajhuri adds that the delay indicated by 'thumma' is purely in mention and that the listener would understand the order even without the particle. The particle is used for a rhetorical purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ثُمَّ يَجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى لا يخفى أنه لا تأخر في وجوب صفاته تعالى، وإلا؛ لكان المتأخّرُ وجوبه حادثاً، وهو محالٌ. وبهذا يُعْلَمُ أن (ثُمَّ) لمجرد الترتيب الذكري - أي: الإخباري - بمعنى: أنه بَعْدَ أن أخبر بصفات السُّلُوب أخير بصفات المعاني، وإنما قَدَّمَ صفاتِ السلوب على صفات المعاني؛ لأن الأولى من قبيل التخلية - بالخاء المعجمة - والثانية من قبيل التحلية - بالحاء المهملة ، والأولى مُقَدَّمَةٌ عرفاً على الثانية؛ إذ الإنسانُ لا يتزيَّن بجميل الثياب ونحوها إلا بعد إزالة ما به من الأوساخ، كداخِلِ الحَمَّام، فإنه يُزِيلُ أَدْرَانَهُ - أي: أوساخه -، ثم يَلْبَسُ ثِيَابَهُ. وإنما أعاد لفظ (يجب) مع تقدمه سابقاً في قوله: (فمما يجب... إلخ) للفصل بقوله: (فهذه ست صفات... إلخ)، وللريّ صريحاً على من نفى وجوب صفات المعاني كالمعتزلة. واعتُرِضَ على المصنف بأن قوله : (ثم يجب له تعالى... إلخ) أَوْجَبَ عدم حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري. (قوله: بِمَعْنَى... إلخ) مفاد هذا: أن ( ثم) للدلالة على تأخر ذكر ما بعدها على ذكر ما قبلها، مع أن هذا التأخر لا يحتاج في فهمه إلى حرف يدلُّ عليه؛ لأن السامع إذا سمع ما قبلها أولاً، وسمع ما بعدها آخراً؛ فهم ضرورة تأخر ذكر ما بعدها عن ذكر ما قبلها، فيتعين أن المراد بالترتيب الذكري استحقاق التأخر الذكري لنكتة ككون ما قبلها من باب التخلية، وما بعدها من باب التحلية. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. (قوله: لأنَّ الأُولَى مِنْ قَبيل التَّخْلِية... إلخ) تقدم ما فيه.
His saying: 'Then (thumma) it is necessary for Him, exalted...' – it is not hidden that there is no delay in the necessity of His attributes, exalted; otherwise, the delayed in its necessity would be originated, which is impossible. And by this it is known that 'thumma' is for mere order of mention – i.e., informative order – meaning that after he informed of the attributes of negations, he informed of the attributes of meanings. And he only presented the attributes of negations before the attributes of meanings because the former are of the category of purification (takhliyah) and the latter are of the category of adornment (tahliyah), and the former is customarily prior to the latter; for a person does not adorn himself with beautiful clothes and the like except after removing what is on him of dirt, like the one entering the bathhouse, for he removes his filth – i.e., his dirt – then puts on his clothes. And he only repeated the word 'it is necessary' (yajibu) despite its preceding earlier in his saying 'among what is necessary...' due to the separation by his saying 'so these are six attributes...' and to clearly refute those who deny the necessity of the attributes of meanings, like the Mu'tazila. And an objection was raised against the author that his saying 'then it is necessary for Him...' necessitated the non-... The Hashiyah of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: (His saying: 'meaning...etc.') The implication of this is that 'thumma' indicates the delay of the mention of what follows it over the mention of what precedes it, even though this delay does not require a particle to indicate it, because the listener, when he hears what precedes it first and hears what follows it last, necessarily understands the delay of the mention of what follows it over the mention of what precedes it. So it is determined that what is meant by 'order of mention' is the entitlement to delay in mention for a purpose, such as the former being of the category of purification and the latter of adornment. The Taqrirat of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi: (His saying: 'because the former are of the category of purification... etc.') What is in it has preceded.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage addresses the word 'thumma' (then) in the text when moving from negative attributes to attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani). The main point is that 'thumma' does not imply temporal delay in the necessity of the attributes, because that would imply the later attributes are originated, which is impossible. Instead, 'thumma' is used for 'order of mention' (al-tartib al-dhikri) or informative order. The reason for presenting negations first is analogized to purification (takhliyah) before adornment (tahliyah): just as one cleans himself before putting on fine clothes, the removal of imperfections (negations) precedes the affirmation of perfections (attributes of meanings). The repetition of the word 'yajibu' (it is necessary) is justified by the intervening text and to explicitly refute the Mu'tazila who deny the necessity of the attributes of meanings. An objection is raised that 'thumma' might imply a temporal necessity, but it is dismissed. Al-Ajhuri's gloss explains that the delay indicated by 'thumma' is purely in mention, not in reality, and the listener would understand the order even without the particle, but it is used for a rhetorical purpose. Al-Anbabi notes that this point has been made earlier. The passage thus defends the logical and rhetorical structure of the text.

Key Terms
ثم
الترتيب الذكري
التخلية
التحلية
صفات المعاني
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the word 'thumma' in 'ثم يجب له تعالى' indicates a temporal delay in the necessity of some of Allah's attributes.
Correction: The passage explains that 'thumma' is for order of mention only; there is no temporal sequence in the necessity of attributes, as that would imply originated attributes.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the word 'thumma' in the phrase 'ثم يجب له تعالى'?
A) To indicate a temporal delay in the necessity of attributes
B) To show that the attributes of meanings are originated
C) To indicate order of mention, not temporal order
D) To separate the negative attributes from the positive ones

Key Takeaway
The word 'thumma' in the transition to the attributes of meanings indicates order of mention, not temporal sequence, and the order of negation before affirmation follows the natural pattern of purification before adornment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own journey of faith, do you tend to rush into 'adornment' (trying to accumulate good deeds or knowledge) without first engaging in 'purification' (removing spiritual dirt and wrong beliefs)? How does the bathhouse analogy in this lesson challenge your current approach?
?
The author repeats the word 'yajibu' (it is necessary) to openly refute the Mu'tazila who denied some divine attributes. Are there any beliefs you hold that you have never examined against the clear statements of the scholars? What would it take for you to stand firm on a truth even if others deny it?
?
When you hear the word 'thumma' in Islamic texts, do you immediately assume a time sequence? How can you train yourself to be more careful with such terms, especially when discussing Allah's attributes, so that you avoid falling into misconceptions about His nature?

Understanding the Five Negative Attributes
Sanusi defines each of the five negative attributes by what they negate, then clarifies their positive nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what it means for an attribute to be 'negative' (salbiyya) and how each of the five attributes negates a specific limitation from Allah.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are not deficiencies; they negate deficiencies from Allah.

In this passage, Imam al-Sanusi explains why five of the essential divine attributes are labeled 'negative.' He shows that each attribute is actually a negation of a certain limitation—such as a beginning or an end—from Allah. Understanding this helps us see that these attributes are real and positive, not absences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise definitions and the key clarification at the end.
2
Identify each attribute and its negation
Find the five attributes mentioned: qidam, baqa', mukhalafah lil-hawadith, qiyam bi nafs, and wahdaniyyah. For each, note what specific limitation it negates from Allah.
The negations are: beginning, end, likeness, need, and multiplicity.
3
Understand the crucial clarification
Sanusi emphasizes that these attributes are called 'negative' because their meaning is the negation of something from Allah, not because they are themselves negated from Him. They are firmly established for Allah.
This prevents misunderstanding that negative attributes imply a lack in Allah.
4
Reflect on the call to ponder
The passage ends with 'fata'dabbar' (so reflect). Why does Sanusi urge reflection? Think about how these negations together affirm Allah's perfection and uniqueness.
Reflection deepens understanding and prevents errors in aqeedah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبيَّةٌ إنما نُسِبَتْ للسلب؛ لأنها مُفَسَّرَةٌ به؛ إذ القِدَمُ: سَلْبُ أوَّليَّة الوجود، والبقاءُ سَلْبُ آخِرِيَّةِ الوجود، والمخالفة للحوادث: سَلْبُ المماثلة لها، والقيام بالنفس سَلْبُ الافتقار والوحدانية: سَلْبُ التعدد. وعُلِمَ من ذلك أن المراد بكونها سلبيةً أن معناها سَلْبُ كذا لا أنها مَسْلُوبَةٌ عن المولى؛ إذ هي ثابتة له لا مسلوبة عنه. فتدبر.
His saying: 'And the five after them are negative (salbiyya).' They are attributed to negation (salb) only because they are interpreted by it. For qidam (eternality) is the negation of the beginning of existence; baqa' (permanence) is the negation of the end of existence; mukhalafah lil-hawadith (dissimilarity to contingent things) is the negation of likeness to them; qiyam bi nafs (self-subsistence) is the negation of need; and wahdaniyyah (oneness) is the negation of multiplicity. And it is understood from this that the intended meaning of their being 'negative' is that their meaning is the negation of such-and-such, not that they are negated from the Lord—for they are established for Him, not negated from Him. So reflect.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage defines the five negative attributes (al-sifāt al-salbiyya) of God. It explains why they are called 'negative': each is interpreted by negating a certain deficiency from God—qidam negates a beginning, baqa' negates an end, mukhalafah negates resemblance to creation, qiyam bi nafs negates need, wahdaniyyah negates multiplicity. The author then clarifies a crucial nuance: these attributes are called 'negative' not because they are themselves negated from God, but because their content is the negation of something from Him. They are real positive attributes established for God. The passage ends with an admonition to reflect (fata'dabbar).

Key Terms
صفات سلبية
القديم
البقاء
المخالفة للحوادث
القيام بالنفس
الوحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that negative attributes mean Allah lacks those attributes, e.g., that qidam is absent from Allah.
Correction: Negative attributes are not absences in Allah; they are positive affirmations that negate their opposites. For example, qidam negates a beginning but itself is a real attribute of Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the attribute of qidam (eternality) negate?
A) The end of existence
B) The beginning of existence
C) Likeness to contingent things
D) Need

Key Takeaway
The five negative attributes are positive attributes that negate limitations from Allah, affirming His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If qidam negates any beginning to Allah's existence, then your existence is a gift from One who never began. Does your daily life recognize this absolute priority of His existence over yours, or do you act as if your life is the center of reality? How can you live with a constant awareness that He alone is eternal?
?
Qiyam bi nafs negates all need from Allah. Yet you cling to people, possessions, and plans as if you cannot survive without them. What would it look like to genuinely internalize that Allah is the only Self-Sufficient, and to realign your dependencies accordingly?
?
Wahdaniyyah negates multiplicity. Where in your heart do you serve multiple 'lords'—fear of people, love of status, pursuit of comfort? How can you consciously affirm Allah's oneness in your decisions today, even in small matters?

Seven vs Eight Attributes: Ash'ari and Maturidi Views
Bajuri states the difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis on the number of essential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi schools regarding the number of essential divine attributes, specifically the Maturidi addition of the attribute of takwin (creative power).

Core Idea
Maturidis add an eighth attribute, takwin, which Ash'aris do not recognize as a separate essential attribute.

The difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi schools on divine attributes is a classic point of kalam. While Ash'aris hold to seven essential attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani), Maturidis add an eighth: takwin, or creative power. This passage from Bajuri's commentary explains how takwin is understood as an eternal attribute that underlies the so-called 'attributes of actions'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Note the key terms: سبع صفات, ثمان صفات, التكوين, صفات الأفعال.
The passage includes marginal notes that clarify the details of takwin's relation to specific actions.
2
Identify the two positions
Notice that Ash'aris affirm seven attributes, while Maturidis affirm eight. Find where the text states this difference.
The eighth attribute is takwin, which is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence.
3
Understand takwin and its effects
The passage explains that takwin is the source for bringing into existence and nonexistence, and it is the basis for the attributes of actions like creation, provision, and giving life.
For Maturidis, these attributes of actions are eternal, not created.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this difference matters: it shows how different schools conceive of God's action and its relation to His essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ) أي عند الأشاعرة، وأما عند الماتريدية؛ فثمان صفاتٍ؛ لأنهم يزيدون على ما سيأتي صِفَةَ التكوين فهي عندهم: صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى بها الإيجادُ ،والإعْدَامُ، وهي المرادَةُ عندهم من صفات الأفعال؛ لأنهم يقولون: إن تعلَّقَتْ بالخلق تسمّى خَلْقاً، وإن تعلَّقَتْ بالرزق تسمّى: رَزْقاً، وإن تعلَّقَتْ بالإحياء تسمّى إحياء، وهكذا. وعلى هذا فصفات الأفعال قديمة. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. (قوله: إِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالْخَلْقِ) أي بوجود من أريد إيجاده. (وقوله: وَإِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالرَّزْقِ) بفتح الراء مصدراً ليطابق ما قبله وما بعده، والمراد: إن تعلقت بأثره، وهو الرزق - بكسر الراء - بمعنى: المرزوق به. (وقوله: وَإِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالْإِحْيَاءِ) أي: بأثره، وهو الحياة.
His saying: 'Seven attributes' i.e., according to the Ash'aris, but according to the Maturidis, there are eight attributes, because they add the attribute of takwin (creative power) to what will come. So it is for them an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted is He, through which bringing into existence (ijad) and bringing into nonexistence (i'dam) occur. It is what is intended by them from the attributes of actions (sifat al-af'al). Because they say: if it attaches to creating, it is called creation; if it attaches to provision, it is called provision; if it attaches to giving life, it is called giving life, and so on. Thus, the attributes of actions are eternal. A note by the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri. Notes by the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi: His saying: 'If it attaches to creation (al-khalq)' means to the existence of one whose existence is intended. His saying: 'And if it attaches to provision (al-rizq)'—with fath on the ra', a verbal noun, to match what precedes and follows—and the intended meaning is if it attaches to its effect, which is provision (al-rizq with kasr on the ra') meaning the thing provided. His saying: 'And if it attaches to giving life (al-ihya')' means to its effect, which is life.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage explains the difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi schools regarding the number of essential divine attributes. For Ash'aris, there are seven attributes of meanings (sifāt al-ma'ānī). Maturidis add an eighth: takwīn (creative power). Takwīn is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence through which He brings things into existence and nonexistence. It is the ground for what are called 'attributes of actions' (sifat al-af'al). When this power attaches to different actions, it is named accordingly: if to creating, it is called 'creation'; if to provision, 'provision'; if to giving life, 'giving life'. Importantly, for the Maturidis, these attributes of actions are themselves eternal. The marginal notes then clarify the details: when takwīn attaches to creation, it means to the existence of the one intended; when to provision, it means to the effect (the provided thing); when to giving life, it means to life.

Key Terms
سبع صفات
ثمان صفات
التكوين
صفات الأفعال
الأشاعرة
الماتريدية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidis have eight attributes because they add an attribute that Ash'aris deny as a possible attribute of God.
Correction: The Maturidis do not deny the reality of the attributes of actions; they simply subsume them under the single eternal attribute of takwin, making it eight essential attributes rather than seven plus created actions.

Checkpoint
How many essential attributes do the Maturidis hold?
A) Seven
B) Eight
C) Six
D) Nine

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis add takwin as an eighth essential attribute, which they see as the eternal source of all actions, while Ash'aris do not consider it a separate essential attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment of your existence depends on God's continuous creative act? How would your daily worries change if you consciously affirmed that your being is sustained by His eternal takwin, not by your own efforts? This week, in each of your five daily prayers, include a moment of silence to acknowledge that you are being recreated anew.
?
The Maturidis teach that God's attribute of takwin takes different names depending on what He does—creating, providing, giving life. Have you ever taken a gift—like a meal, a breath, a new day—without recognizing it as a direct expression of His eternal creative power? Today, before you eat, drink, or sleep, pause and say: 'This is not just a thing; this is takwin in action.' Will you commit to this practice for the next seven days?

Seven or Eight? The Ash'ari-Maturidi Difference on Divine Attributes
Explains the difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis on the number of attributes and the nature of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidis count eight eternal attributes while Ash'aris count seven, and the nature of the attribute of takwin.

Core Idea
Maturidis add takwin: one eternal attribute with many effects.

When studying the divine attributes, you will encounter a classical difference between the two Sunni schools of kalam. The Ash'aris hold that there are seven eternal attributes of meaning (sifaat al-ma'ani). The Maturidis, however, count eight, adding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). This lesson explains the Maturidi view and how takwin relates to what are called 'attributes of actions'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two positions: Ash'aris say seven, Maturidis say eight.
2
Understand the Maturidi argument
The Maturidis add takwin as an eternal attribute. See how they argue that it is the source of all 'attributes of actions' like creating, providing, and giving life.
Takwin is a single attribute with multiple relational effects.
3
Examine the gloss by al-Ajhuri
The gloss clarifies that when takwin relates to creation, it is called 'creation'; when to provision, 'provision'; when to life, 'giving life'. This shows the unity of the attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ) أي عند الأشاعرة، وأما عند الماتريدية؛ فثمان صفاتٍ؛ لأنهم يزيدون على ما سيأتي صِفَةَ التكوين فهي عندهم: صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى بها الإيجادُ ،والإعْدَامُ، وهي المرادَةُ عندهم من صفات الأفعال؛ لأنهم يقولون: إن تعلَّقَتْ بالخلق تسمّى خَلْقاً، وإن تعلَّقَتْ بالرزق تسمّى: رَزْقاً، وإن تعلَّقَتْ بالإحياء تسمّى إحياء، وهكذا. وعلى هذا فصفات الأفعال قديمة. . حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: إِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالْخَلْقِ) أي بوجود من أريد إيجاده. (وقوله: وَإِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالرَّزْقِ) بفتح الراء مصدراً ليطابق ما قبله وما بعده، والمراد: إن تعلقت بأثره، وهو الرزق - بكسر الراء - بمعنى: المرزوق به. (وقوله: وَإِنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِالْإِحْيَاءِ) أي: بأثره، وهو الحياة.
His statement: 'Seven attributes' – meaning according to the Ash'aris, but according to the Maturidis, there are eight attributes, because they add to what will come the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). So for them, it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted be He, by which existence and non-existence are effected, and it is intended by them from the attributes of actions because they say: if it is related to creation, it is called 'creation'; if related to provision, it is called 'provision'; if related to giving life, it is called 'giving life', and so on. And on this, the attributes of actions are eternal. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: (His statement: 'If it is related to creation') – i.e., to the existence of the one intended to be created. (And his statement: 'And if it is related to provision') – with fatha on the ra' as a verbal noun to match what precedes and follows, and the meaning: if it is related to its effect, which is provision (rizq with kasr of ra') meaning the provisioned thing. (And his statement: 'And if it is related to giving life') – i.e., to its effect, which is life.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a definition and sectarian comparison. It first clarifies that the statement 'seven attributes' refers to the Ash'ari position. It then explains that the Maturidis hold there are eight attributes because they add the attribute of takwin (efficient causation). This attribute is eternal and subsisting in God's essence, and it is the source of all so-called 'attributes of actions' like creating, providing, giving life, etc., depending on its relation to different effects. Thus, the Maturidis consider the attributes of actions eternal, not created. The gloss by al-Ajhuri clarifies the terms: the attribute of takwin relates to bringing existence into being; provision is a verbal noun meaning the act of providing, and it relates to its effect (the provisioned thing); giving life relates to its effect (life). This emphasizes that takwin is a single attribute with multiple relational effects.

Key Terms

صفة التكوين
صفات الأفعال

Misconception: Some think that Maturidis and Ash'aris agree on seven attributes, or that takwin is a created attribute.
Correction: Maturidis hold that takwin is an eternal attribute of God, distinct from the seven, making eight attributes. The attributes of actions are expressions of takwin's relations.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis add the attribute of takwin as an eighth eternal attribute, considering the attributes of actions as its relational expressions.

How would your trust in God deepen if you consistently lived by this truth?
?
The Maturidis insist that takwin is eternal and not a created act. Do you ever think of God's actions as if they were like human actions—temporal and reactive? What would it mean for your worship to remember that God's power to bring things about is not a series of separate decisions but the expression of one eternal, unchanging attribute?
?

Does this realization make you more aware that you are constantly being sustained by God's single, unceasing will? How can you cultivate a constant sense of dependence on that one attribute rather than worrying about each separate need in isolation?

Ash'ari View on Attributes of Actions and the Function of Power
Argues that the Ash'ari view is preferable and answers a Maturidi objection about the function of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash‘ari position on attributes of actions as created relational accidents and how they answer the Maturidi objection regarding the function of divine power.

Core Idea
Attributes of actions are created relational accidents of power, not distinct eternal attributes.

This passage presents the preferred Ash‘ari view on the nature of attributes of actions. It then addresses a key Maturidi objection about the role of divine power, showing a sophisticated dialectic about possibility and readiness. Follow along as the argument unfolds step by step.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Ash'ari position
Read the opening statement carefully. The Ash‘aris deny an additional attribute of takwin and define attributes of actions as the created relational accidents of power in actual exercise.
Note that 'relational accidents' (ta‘alluqāt) are not attributes subsisting in the essence but momentary relations.
2
Encounter the Maturidi objection
The objection asks: if takwin is what effects existence and non-existence, what function remains for power? This frames the entire dialectic.
Take a moment to think about why the Maturidi might see a redundancy.
3
Follow the first answer and its rebuttal
The Maturidi answer is that power prepares the possible. But the objector points out that the possible is intrinsically receptive, so preparation is unnecessary.
This is the key pivot: intrinsic vs. acquired readiness.
4
Understand the final refinement
The Ash‘ari response clarifies that power gives a special readiness (qubūl isti‘dād) beyond the intrinsic receptivity. The commentator adds 'ta’ammal' – reflect.
Consider why this resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراجح مذهب الأشاعرة من عدم زيادة تلك الصفة، ومن كَوْنِ المراد من صفات الأفعال: تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية، وتلك التعلقات حادثة، وعلى هذا فصفاتُ الأفعال حادثة فإن قيل : إذا كانت صفة التكوين بها الإيجادُ والإعدام عند الماتريدية، فما وظيفةُ القدرة عندهم؟ أجيب بأن وظيفتها: تهيئة الممكن للوجود والعدم، بمعنى: جعله قابلاً لذلك. ويُحِثَ في هذا الجواب بأن الممكن قابل لذلك في ذاته، فلا حاجة إلى تهيئة القدرة له وأجيب بأن المراد: أنها تَجْعَلُهُ قابلاً لذلك قبول استعداد؛ وإن كان قابلاً لذلك قبولاً ذاتياً. فتأمل.
And the preferable (al-rājiḥ) is the school of the Ash'aris in not adding that attribute, and in that the intended meaning from the attributes of actions is the relational accidents (taʿalluqāt) of power in its actual exercise (al-tanjīziyya), and those relational accidents are created (ḥāditha). On this basis, the attributes of actions are created. So if it is said: If the attribute of takwin (bringing into being) is that by which existence and non-existence are effected according to the Maturidis, then what is the function of power according to them? The answer is: its function is to prepare the possible for existence and non-existence, meaning: to make it receptive for that. It is objected to this answer that the possible is in itself receptive for that, so there is no need for power to prepare it. And it is answered that the meaning is that it makes it receptive for that with a receptive readiness (qubūl istiʿdād); even though it is receptive with an intrinsic receptivity (qubūl dhātī). Reflect.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation argument. It states that the preferable (al-rājiḥ) view is the Ash'ari position: there is no increase of the attribute of takwin (i.e., it is not a distinct attribute), and what are called 'attributes of actions' are actually the relational accidents (taʿalluqāt) of power in its actual exercise (al-tanjīziyya). These relational accidents are created (ḥāditha), so the attributes of actions are created. Then an objection is raised from the Maturidi perspective: if the attribute of takwin is the one that effects existence and non-existence, what then is the function of power (qudra) according to them? The Maturidi answer is that power's function is to prepare (tahyi'a) the possible for existence or non-existence, i.e., to make it receptive. This answer is objected to: the possible is already intrinsically receptive, so no need for power to prepare it. A second answer is given: power makes it receptive with a receptive readiness (qubūl istiʿdād), even though it has an intrinsic receptivity (qubūl dhātī). The commentator then says 'reflect' (ta'ammal), inviting careful consideration.

Correction: The Ash'ari response shows that the possible already has intrinsic receptivity, so power must add a further readiness; otherwise power would be superfluous.

Attributes of Actions and the Function of Divine Power
Sanusi states Ash'ari view on attributes of actions and defends against a Maturidi objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that attributes of actions are the originated temporal relations of divine power, and the subtle distinction between essential and dispositive receptivity in the function of qudra.

Core Idea
Attributes of actions are not separate attributes but the temporal relations of power.

This passage tackles a key point of difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis: whether there is an attribute of takwin separate from qudra. Sanusi first clarifies the Ash'ari view that attributes of actions are nothing but the temporal relations of power, which are originated. Then he presents and answers a Maturidi objection about the function of qudra, leading to a refined understanding of how power prepares possibilities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi states the Ash'ari position and then presents an objection and two answers.
The passage ends with 'so reflect' – it invites deeper thought.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position
Find the statement that there is no increase in the attribute (takwin beyond qudra) and that attributes of actions are the temporal relations of power. Note that these relations are originated.
This is the core of the Ash'ari view.
3
Follow the objection and response
The Maturidi objection asks: if takwin does the creating, what does qudra do? The first answer: qudra prepares the possible. The objection: the possible is already receptive. The second answer: qudra gives a dispositive receptivity beyond essential receptivity.
The second answer resolves the objection.
4
Reflect on the subtle distinction
Consider the difference between essential receptivity (the possible is inherently able to exist or not) and dispositive receptivity (an extra readiness imparted by power). Reflect on why Sanusi ends with 'ta'ammal'.
This distinction is key to Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراجح مذهب الأشاعرة من عدم زيادة تلك الصفة، ومن كَوْنِ المراد من صفات الأفعال: تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية، وتلك التعلقات حادثة، وعلى هذا فصفاتُ الأفعال حادثة فإن قيل : إذا كانت صفة التكوين بها الإيجادُ والإعدام عند الماتريدية، فما وظيفةُ القدرة عندهم؟ أجيب بأن وظيفتها: تهيئة الممكن للوجود والعدم، بمعنى: جعله قابلاً لذلك. ويُحِثَ[؟] في هذا الجواب بأن الممكن قابل لذلك في ذاته، فلا حاجة إلى تهيئة القدرة له وأجيب بأن المراد: أنها تَجْعَلُهُ قابلاً لذلك قبول استعداد؛ وإن كان قابلاً لذلك قبولاً ذاتياً. فتأمل.
And the preponderant (view) is the school of the Ash'aris: that there is no increase in that attribute (i.e., takwin as distinct from qudra), and that what is meant by attributes of actions is the temporal relations of power (ta'alluqāt al-qudrat al-tanjīziyya), and those relations are originated (ḥāditha). Upon this, the attributes of actions are originated. If it is said: 'If the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) is that by which existence and non-existence occur according to the Maturidis, then what is the function of power (qudra) according to them?' It is answered: Its function is preparing the possible (mumkin) for existence and non-existence, meaning: making it receptive to that. It is objected [؟] to this answer that the possible is receptive to that in its essence, so there is no need for power to prepare it. And it is answered: What is meant is that it makes it receptive to that with a receptivity of disposition (qabūl isti'dād), even if it is receptive to that with an essential receptivity. So reflect.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument regarding the difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi views on divine attributes. It begins by stating the preponderant (rājiḥ) Ash'ari position: there is no additional attribute of takwin beyond qudra; rather, the so-called 'attributes of actions' are nothing but the temporal relations (ta'alluqāt tanjīziyya) of power, which are originated (ḥāditha). This makes the attributes of actions themselves originated. Then an objection is raised from the Maturidi perspective: if takwin is the attribute that actually creates and annihilates, what function remains for power? The answer given is that power's function is to prepare the possible (mumkin) for existence or non-existence, making it receptive. A further objection follows: the possible is already receptive in its essence, so no preparation is needed. The final answer refines this: power makes it receptive with a receptivity of disposition (qabūl isti'dād), which is additional to its essential receptivity. The passage ends with 'ta'ammal' (reflect), inviting the reader to ponder the subtlety.

Correction: The text clarifies that the preparation by qudra is for a dispositive receptivity (isti'dād) beyond the essential receptivity, thus preserving a distinct function for qudra.

Definition of Qudra and Its Two Relations
Sanusi defines qudra and explains its two types of ta'alluq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine power (qudra) as a positive attribute and its two types of relation: primordial (ṣulūḥī) and temporal (tanjīzī), and how this distinction reconciles a theological dispute.

Core Idea
Divine power has two relations: eternal suitability and temporal actuality.

Sanusi begins by defining the divine attribute of power, clarifying that its primary relation is the eternal suitability to create or annihilate every possible, not the actual creation. This distinction resolves a disagreement among scholars about whether things that never exist, like Abi Jahl's faith, are within God's power. Read carefully to grasp this foundational concept in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Note the technical terms.
2
Identify the definition of qudra
Find the definition of qudra as an attribute subsisting in God's essence and how it relates to every possible.
The definition points to the primordial relation.
3
Distinguish the two relations
Notice the two types of ta'alluq: the primordial (ṣulūḥī) eternal and the temporal (tanjīzī) originated. Understand the difference.
The text uses 'yata'atta' to indicate the primordial.
4
Understand the reconciliation
See how this distinction reconciles the dispute over whether something like Abi Jahl's faith is maqdūr.
One says yes (primordial), one says no (temporal).
5
Note the two summary relations
The passage concludes that power has two relations in summary, but seven in detail. The first two are explained.
The text cuts off after the second relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَهِيَ) أي: السبعُ صفات التي تسمى: صفاتِ المعاني. (وقوله: الْقُدْرَةُ) هي صفةً وجودية قائمة بذاته تعالى يتأتى بها إيجاد كلّ مُمْكِن وإعدامه إشارة إلى تعلقها الصُّلُوحِيَ القديم. وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام، لا إلى تعلقها التنجيزي الحادث، وهو الإيجاد والإعدام بالفعل؛ لأن المتبادِرَ من التعبير بالتأتي هو الأول، وأيضاً التعبير ب: كل ممكن يقتضيه؛ لأنها تتعلق تعلقاً تنجيزياً حادثاً بكل ممكن؛ إذ الممكنُ الذي تعلَّقَ عِلْمُ الله تعالى بعدم وجوده كإيمان أبي جهل؛ لا تتعلَّق ذلك التعلُّق؛ وإن تعلَّقَتْ به تعلُّقاً صُلُوحيّاً قديماً، وبهذا جُمِعَ بين الخلاف في كونه مقدوراً أو غير مقدور، فحُمِلَ الأول على التعلق الصلوحي القديم، والثاني على التعلق التنجيزي الحادث. به فتلخص أن للقدرة تعلُّقين: أحدهما: صلوحي قديم، والآخر: تنجيزي حادث، لكن هذا على سبيل الإجمال. وأما على سبيل التفصيل؛ فلها سبعة (١) تعلقات: الأول: الصلوحي القديم، وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام. والثاني: كَوْنُ الممكن فيما لا يزالُ قبل وجوده في قَبْضَةِ القدرة، بمعنى: أن الله
(His saying: 'and they' (wa hiya) means the seven attributes that are called attributes of meanings. And his saying: 'al-qudra (power)' is an positive attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted, by which is effected the bringing into existence of every possible (mumkin) and its annihilating, an indication of its primordial (ṣulūḥī) eternal relation (ta'alluq). And it is its suitability in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and annihilating, not its temporal (tanjīzī) originated relation, which is the actual bringing into existence and annihilating; because what is understood from the expression 'by which is effected' (yata'atta) is the first, and also the expression 'every possible' necessitates it; because it relates with a temporal originated relation to every possible? But the possible which God's knowledge has attached to its non-existence, like the faith of Abi Jahl, does not have that relation; rather, it has a primordial eternal relation to it. And by this, a reconciliation is made between the disagreement over whether it is power-able (maqdūr) or not; so the first is interpreted as the primordial eternal relation, and the second as the temporal originated relation. Through this, it is concluded that power has two relations: one primordial eternal, and the other temporal originated, but this is in summary. As for in detail, it has seven relations: the first: the primordial eternal, which is its suitability in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and annihilating. The second: the being of the possible in what is yet to come, before its existence, in the grasp of power, meaning that God...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of power (qudra) and explains its two fundamental relations. It begins by identifying 'they' in the text as the seven attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma'ānī). Then defines qudra as a positive (wujūdiyya) attribute subsisting in God's essence, by which every possible (mumkin) is brought into existence and annihilated. The definition points to its primordial (ṣulūḥī) eternal relation, meaning its suitability in pre-eternity to create and destroy, not the temporal (tanjīzī) relation which is the actual act. This is because the wording 'yata'atta' (is effected) suggests the first, and also the phrase 'every possible' requires it, because power relates with a temporal relation to every possible? But a possible that God knows will never exist, like the faith of Abi Jahl, has no temporal relation; it only has the primordial relation. This reconciles the dispute over whether such a thing is 'powered' (maqdūr): the first opinion refers to the primordial relation, the second to the temporal. The passage then summarizes that power has two relations: primordial eternal and temporal originated. But in detail, there are seven relations: the first is the primordial eternal (suitability in pre-eternity), and the second is the possible being in the grasp of power before its existence in the future. The text cuts off here, but the enumeration continues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that divine power actually creates every possible thing that can be conceived, including those that will never exist.
Correction: The text clarifies that power has two relations: the primordial relation includes all possibilities eternally, but the temporal relation only applies to things that actually come into existence. So, the power of God is not actualized for things that never exist, but He has the eternal ability to bring them about if He willed.

The Two Attachments of Divine Power
Al-Bajuri distinguishes two types of power attachment and resolves a theological dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the pre-dispositive eternal attachment and the temporal executive attachment of divine power, and how this resolves a theological disagreement over whether impossible things are within power.

Core Idea
Power has two attachments: eternal suitability and actual action.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies a key distinction in the nature of divine power. Before we can understand how God's power relates to all possible things, we must separate two very different types of attachment: one that is eternal and potential, and another that is temporal and actual. This distinction solves a famous disagreement over whether things that never exist are 'within power'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Bajuri introduces the two attachments by contrasting them.
Pay attention to the terms 'ṣulūḥī qadīm' and 'tanjīzī ḥādith'.
2
Identify the two attachments
The passage first defines the pre-dispositive attachment as suitability, then the executive as actual action. Identify the example of Abu Jahl's faith and see how it illustrates the difference.
The expression 'al-ta'atti' (suitability) is key to understanding the first attachment.
3
Understand the reconciliation
The passage resolves a disagreement: those who say a non-existent possible is 'maqdūr' mean by the pre-dispositive attachment, those who deny mean by the executive. Confirm this by re-reading the last few lines.
This shows how careful distinctions in kalam prevent confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام، لا إلى تعلقها التنجيزي الحادث، وهو الإيجاد والإعدام بالفعل؛ لأن المتبادِرَ من التعبير بالتأتي هو الأول، وأيضاً التعبير ب: كل ممكن يقتضيه؛ لأنها تتعلق تعلقاً تنجيزياً حادثاً بكل ممكن؛ إذ الممكنُ الذي تعلَّقَ عِلْمُ الله تعالى بعدم وجوده كإيمان أبي جهل؛ لا تتعلَّق ذلك التعلُّق؛ وإن تعلَّقَتْ به تعلُّقاً صُلُواحيّاً قديماً، وبهذا جُمِعَ بين الخلاف في كونه مقدوراً أو غير مقدور، فحُمِلَ الأول على التعلق الصلوحي القديم، والثاني على التعلق التنجيزي الحادث. فتلخص أن للقدرة تعلُّقين: أحدهما: صلوحي قديم، والآخر: تنجيزي حادث، لكن هذا على سبيل الإجمال. وأما على سبيل التفصيل؛ فلها سبعة تعلقات: الأول: الصلوحي القديم، وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام. والثاني: كَوْنُ الممكن فيما لا يزالُ قبل وجوده في قَبْضَةِ القدرة، بمعنى: أن الله متن أم البراهين لأبي عبد الله السنوسي تعالى إن شاء أبقاه على عدمه، وإن شاء أَوْجَده بها، وهو من أقسام تعلقات القبضة. الثالثُ: إيجادُ الله تعالى الشيء بها فيما لا يزال، وهو من أقسام التعلق التنجيزي الحادث. والرابعُ : كَوْنُ الممكن حالة وجوده في قبضة القدرة، بمعنى: أن الله تعالى إن شاء أبقاه على وجوده، وإن شاء أعدمه بها، وهو من أقسام تعلقات القبضة. والخامس: إعدام الله الشيء بها، وهو من أقسام التعلق التنجيزي الحادث. والسادس: كَوْنُ الممكن حالة عَدَمِهِ في قبضة القدرة، بمعنى: أن الله تعالى إن شاء أبقاه على عدمه، وإن شاء أوجده بها، وهو من أقسام تعلقات القبضة. والسابع: إيجادُ الله الشيء بها حين البعث، وهو من أقسام التعلق التنجيزي الحادث. هذا، وسكتوا عن تعلقها بالشيء بعد ذلك، وهو كَوْنُهُ في قبضة القدرة، بمعنى: أن الله إن شاء أبقاه على وجوده، وإن شاء أعدمه بها بقطع النظر عن الأدلة الشرعية الواردة في ذلك، فإذا ضُمَّ هذا التعلق إلى السبعة السابقة؛ كانت الجملة ثمانية.
And it (power's salahi attachment) is its suitability in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and causing nonexistence, not to its temporal executive attachment, which is the actual bringing into existence and causing nonexistence; because the immediate understanding from the expression 'suitability' (al-ta'atti) is the first, and also the expression 'every possible requires it' because it attaches with a temporal executive attachment to every possible; indeed the possible which God's knowledge has attached to its nonexistence, like the faith of Abū Jahl, it (power) does not have that (executive) attachment; although it has a pre-dispositive eternal attachment (ta'alluq ṣulūḥī qadīm). And by this a reconciliation is made between the disagreement concerning whether it is within power (maqdūr) or not within power; so the first (claim) is interpreted as the pre-dispositive eternal attachment, and the second as the temporal executive attachment. So it is concluded that for power there are two attachments: one: pre-dispositive eternal, the other: temporal executive, but this is in summary. As for in detail, it has seven attachments: the first: the pre-dispositive eternal, which is its suitability in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and causing nonexistence. The second: the possible's being in the grasp of power (qabḍat al-qudra) in the future before its existence, meaning: that God—the text of Umm al-Barāhīn by Abī 'Abd Allāh al-Sanūsī—mighty and sublime, if He wills He keeps it in its nonexistence, and if He wills He brings it into existence by it (power), and it is one of the attachments of the grasp. The third: God's bringing the thing into existence by it in the future, and it is an attachment of the temporal executive type. The fourth: the possible's being in the grasp of power at the time of its existence, meaning: that God, mighty and sublime, if He wills He keeps it in its existence, and if He wills He causes its nonexistence by it, and it is of the attachments of the grasp. The fifth: God's causing the thing's nonexistence by it, and it is of the temporal executive attachments. The sixth: the possible's being in the grasp of power at the time of its nonexistence, meaning: that God, mighty and sublime, if He wills He keeps it in its nonexistence, and if He wills He brings it into existence by it, and it is of the attachments of the grasp. The seventh: God's bringing the thing into existence by it at the time of resurrection, and it is of the temporal executive attachments. This, and they (the scholars) remained silent about its attachment to the thing after that, which is its being in the grasp of power, meaning: that God if He wills He keeps it in its existence, and if He wills He causes its nonexistence by it, disregarding the revealed evidences concerning that. So if this attachment is added to the preceding seven, the total becomes eight.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the attachments of divine power (qudra) from al-Bajuri's commentary on Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin. It begins by clarifying the two main types of attachment: the pre-dispositive eternal attachment (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), which is power's suitability in pre-eternity to create or annihilate, and the temporal executive attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith), which is the actual act of creation or annihilation. The author notes that the term 'suitability' (al-ta'atti) naturally refers to the first, and that when it is said 'every possible requires it,' this refers to the executive attachment—except for possibles that God knows will never exist, like the faith of Abu Jahl, which only have the pre-dispositive attachment. This distinction resolves a disagreement: those who say such a possible is within power (maqdūr) mean by the pre-dispositive attachment, while those who deny it mean by the executive attachment. Al-Bajuri then summarizes: power has two attachments in general, but in detail it has seven (with an implied eighth). The first is the eternal pre-dispositive attachment. The second to the fifth are subtypes of the 'grasp of power' (qabḍat al-qudra): before existence (future preservation in non‑existence or actual creation), during existence (preservation or annihilation), and during non‑existence after creation (preservation in non‑existence or recreation). The sixth and seventh are executive: causing non‑existence and resurrection. The scholars also mention an eighth attachment: the state of the thing after its existence, where God may preserve or annihilate it, independent of revealed evidence. Thus the total attachments of power are eight.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
الصلوحي القديم (al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm)
التنجيزي الحادث (al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith)
المقدور (al-maqdūr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine power either attaches or not, but the passage shows two distinct types.
Correction: Power has both an eternal suitability and a temporal actuality; both are real attachments serving different purposes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the faith of Abu Jahl not subject to the temporal executive attachment of power?
A) Because Abu Jahl never existed.
B) Because God's knowledge attached to its nonexistence.
C) Because it is not a possible thing.
D) Because power only has a pre-dispositive attachment to it.

Key Takeaway
The two-attachment model of power resolves the question of whether impossible things are within power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does knowing that God's power has two attachments—including one that makes possible even what He knows will never happen—change your sense of your own limitations? Can you name a specific situation where you have assumed something is impossible for God, when really it is within His pre-dispositive power? What would it look like to truly believe that today?
?
When you consider that God's power attaches to every possible thing, even those that contradict His foreknowledge (like your own past failures or potential future sins), does that make you feel more accountable or less? Are you tempted to use 'God knew it would happen' as an excuse, or does this drive you to align your choices with what is actually good?
?
The passage resolves a dispute by showing that both sides are correct if you consider the right attachment. Where in your own faith do you slip into oversimplification by saying something is either 'possible' or 'impossible' without considering a deeper truth? What would it cost you to hold both truths together?

The Seven Detailed Attachments of Power
Al-Bajuri enumerates seven detailed attachments of power, with an implied eighth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the seven detailed attachments of divine power and understand their classification into pre-dispositive, grasp (qabḍa), and executive types.

Core Idea
Power has seven attachments in detail: one eternal, three grasp states, and three executive acts.

After summarizing the two main types, al-Bajuri provides a detailed enumeration of seven attachments of power. These include the eternal pre-dispositive attachment, various states of the possible being in the 'grasp of power', and the actual acts of creation, annihilation, and resurrection. An eighth attachment is also mentioned by implication.

Guided Path
1
Read and list the seven attachments
Read the Arabic passage and the translation. As you read, write down each of the seven attachments in order.
Notice that the first is the pre-dispositive eternal; the second, fourth, and sixth are grasp states; the third, fifth, and seventh are executive.
2
Categorize them into groups
Group the attachments: one pre-dispositive, three grasp (before existence, during existence, after death), and three executive (creation, annihilation, resurrection).
The grasp attachments are states of possibility, while executive are actual acts.
3
Understand the eighth attachment
The passage ends by mentioning an implied eighth attachment: the thing's being in the grasp of power after its existence (preservation or annihilation). Note why scholars remained silent.
This eighth attachment is similar to the fourth but without regard to revealed evidence.

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the attachments of divine power (qudra) from al-Bajuri's commentary on Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin. It begins by clarifying the two main types of attachment: the pre-dispositive eternal attachment (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), which is power's suitability in pre-eternity to create or annihilate, and the temporal executive attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith), which is the actual act of creation or annihilation. Misconception: Some might think the grasp of power is the same as the executive attachment.
Correction: The grasp attachments are states of possibility (God can do either), while executive attachments are actual acts of creation, annihilation, or resurrection.

?

The Divine Will: Definition and Its Attachments
Al-Bajuri defines the divine will and distinguishes its two executive attachments from the pre-dispositive one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine will as an attribute that specifies the possible, and the distinction between its executive attachments (eternal and originated) and the pre-dispositive attachment that it lacks.

Core Idea
Unlike power, the divine will has only executive attachments, not a pre-dispositive one.

In this passage, al-Bajuri explains the attribute of will (al-irāda) as defined by the mutakallimūn. He then clarifies a key nuance: the will's specification of possibilities is always actual, never merely potential. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the key terms and the flow of the definition.
2
Identify the definition and the key term 'specifies'
The passage defines will as an attribute that 'specifies' (tukhaṣṣiṣu) the possible. Note that this specification is the core function of the will.
The term 'takhṣīṣ' is central to understanding the attachments.
3
Distinguish the three attachments
The passage describes two executive attachments (eternal and originated) and explicitly excludes a pre-dispositive attachment. Understand why the pre-dispositive is not applicable to will.
This distinction is crucial for differentiating will from power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
:(قوله: (والإرادة) هى صِفَةٌ وجودية قائمة بذاته تعالى تُخَصِّصُ الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه. كذا قال المتكلمون وفي قولهم تُخَصِصُ الممكن... إلخ إشارة إلى تعلقها التنجيزي القديم، وهو تخصيص شيء ببعض ما يجوز عليه أَزَلاً، أو إلى تعلقها التنجيزي الحادِثِ بناءً على القول به، وهو تخصيص الشيء بذلك حين إيجاده وإعدامه، لا إلى تعلقه الصُّلُوحِيّ القديم، وهو صلاحيتها أزلاً لتخصيص الممكن بكلّ شيءٍ مما جاز عليه .
His statement: 'And the will (al-irāda) is an existing attribute subsisting in His essence, may He be exalted, that specifies the possible (al-mumkin) with some of what is permissible for it.' Thus said the mutakallimūn. And in their statement 'specifies the possible... etc.' there is an indication to its temporal executive attachment which is eternal (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), which is the specification of a thing with some of what is permissible for it eternally, or to its temporal executive attachment which is originated (al-ḥādith) based on the affirmation of it, which is the specification of the thing with that at the time of its bringing into existence and causing its nonexistence, not to its pre-dispositive eternal attachment (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), which is its suitability eternally for specifying the possible with every thing from what is permissible for it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the divine attribute of will (al-irāda) from al-Bajuri's commentary. It begins by quoting Sanusi's matn: 'Will is an existing attribute subsisting in God's essence, that specifies the possible with some of what is permissible for it.' The mutakallimun (theologians) have defined it thus. Al-Bajuri then explains that the phrase 'specifies the possible...' indicates one of two types of attachment: either the eternal temporal executive attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), which is God's eternal specification of a thing from pre-eternity, or the originated temporal executive attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith), which is the specification at the moment of bringing into existence or causing nonexistence (this latter is based on the acceptance of a originated attachment). Importantly, the definition does NOT refer to a pre-dispositive eternal attachment (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), which would be the will's eternal suitability to specify the possible with any of its permissible states. Thus, unlike power, will does not have a purely potential pre-dispositive attachment; rather, its attachments are always executive, either eternal (pre‑eternal decree) or temporal (actual specification at the time of action).

Key Terms
الإرادة (al-irāda)
التخصيص (al-takhṣīṣ)
التعلق التنجيزي القديم (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm)
التعلق التنجيزي الحادث (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith)
التعلق الصلوحي القديم (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume that will, like power, has a pre-dispositive eternal attachment (i.e., a potential to specify without actually specifying).
Correction: The passage explicitly denies this: will only has executive attachments (eternal or originated). The will's specification is always actual, never merely potential.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what types of attachment does the divine will have?
A) Only a pre-dispositive eternal attachment.
B) Only a temporal executive attachment.
C) Two executive attachments (eternal and originated) and no pre-dispositive attachment.
D) Both a pre-dispositive and a temporal executive attachment.

Key Takeaway
The divine will specifies possibilities perpetually and actually; it has no merely potential (pre-dispositive) attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's will is always actually specifying every possible thing, what does that mean for the events in your life that you consider random or insignificant? How should this change your trust in His planning?
?
Knowing that the divine will has no mere potential—it always determines a specific outcome—how does that confront your own hesitation and indecision? What area of your life do you need to submit more fully to His actual will?
?
The passage teaches that Allah's will is eternally specifying some possibilities and not others. Are there desires you hold onto that you know contradict His specified will? What would it look like to surrender them today, not just intellectually but in your heart's attachment?

The Attachments of the Divine Will: Three or Two?
Al-Bajuri discusses the number of attachments of the divine will and the metaphorical attribution of action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over the number of attachments of the divine will and why attributing specification to attributes is a mental metaphor.

Core Idea
The will's attachments are two, not three — and all action belongs to Allah alone.

This passage from Al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies a key debate in Ash'ari theology: how many attachments does the divine will have? He shows that while some hold there are three, the verified position is two, and explains why attributing specification to the will or effect to power is metaphorical — the real doer is Allah's Essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without translation. Notice the flow from discussing 'specification' to concluding about attachments.
There is a footnote marker (۱) in the Arabic.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the statement about three attachments based on temporal actualizing attachment, and then the verification that there are only two.
3
Understand the metaphor explanation
Al-Bajuri explains that attributing specification to the will and effect to power is mental metaphor. Ask why he says this.
He connects it to the principle that only Allah's Essence truly acts.
4
Reflect on the takeaway
Consider how this preserves tawhid by not assigning independent creative power to attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن المتبادِرَ من التعبير بالتخصيص أن المراد التخصيص بالفعل، وأيضاً التعبير بـ: بعض ما يجوز عليه يقتضيه؛ لأنها تَصْلُحُ في الأزل لتخصيص الممكن بكلّ شيءٍ مما جاز عليه لا بالبعض فقط . فتلخص أن للإرادة ثلاثة (۱) تعلقات بناءً على القول بأن لها تعلقاً تنجيزياً حادثاً. والتحقيق: أن ذلك ليس تعلقاً مستقلاً، بل إظهار للتعلق التنجيزي القديم، وعلى هذا فيكون لها تعلُّقان فقط: أحدهما: صلوحي قديم، والآخرُ: تنجيزي قديم، وإسنادُ التخصيص إليها مجاز عقلي من الإسناد إلى السبب، وإلا؛ فالمخصص حقيقة هو الذاتُ الأَقْدَسُ، وكذلك إسنادُ التأثير إلى القدرة في قول بعضهم: هي صفةٌ تُؤَثِرُ في الممكن الوجود أو العدم، فهو مجاز عقلي من باب الإسناد إلى السبب، وإلا فالمؤثِرُ حقيقةً هو الذاتُ الأقدسُ ؛ إذ لا فِعْلَ إلا له كما نص عليه غيرُ واحد من المحققين.
Because the common understanding from the expression 'specification' is that what is meant is specification by action, and also the expression 'some of what is permissible upon Him' necessitates it because it is suitable in pre-eternity for specifying the possible with everything that is permissible upon it, not only some. So it follows that the will has three attachments based on the statement that it has a temporal actualizing attachment. But the verification is that this is not an independent attachment, rather it is a manifestation of the eternal actualizing attachment; and on this basis it has only two attachments: one is an eternal potential attachment, and the other is an eternal actualizing attachment. Attributing specification to it is a mental metaphor of attribution to the cause; otherwise, the real specifier is the Most Holy Essence. Likewise, attributing effect to power in the statement of some: 'It is an attribute that effects existence or non-existence in the possible' is a mental metaphor of the type of attribution to the cause; otherwise, the real efficient is the Most Holy Essence, for there is no act except His, as more than one of the verifying scholars have stated.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage by Al-Bajuri is an analytical explanation of the term 'specification' (takhsis) in relation to the divine will. He begins by noting that the common understanding of 'specification' implies an action, and that the expression 'some of what is permissible upon Him' necessitates that the will is suitable in pre-eternity for specifying any possible with any aspect that is permissible, not just some aspects. From this, he concludes that the will has three attachments if one holds that it has a temporal actualizing attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith). However, the verified truth (tahqiq) is that this temporal attachment is not independent; rather, it is a manifestation of the eternal actualizing attachment. Thus, there are only two attachments: an eternal potential attachment and an eternal actualizing attachment. Then Al-Bajuri clarifies that attributing specification to the will is a mental metaphor, because the real specifier is the divine Essence. Similarly, attributing effect (ta'thir) to God's power (qudra) is also a mental metaphor, because the real agent is the Essence alone, as established by the verifying scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The divine will or power independently causes specification or effect without Allah's Essence.
Correction: Al-Bajuri shows that attributing action to attributes is metaphorical; the real cause is the Most Holy Essence.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, why is attributing specification to the divine will considered a mental metaphor?
A) Because the will is not a real attribute
B) Because the real specifier is the divine Essence
C) Because the will only has potential attachments
D) Because specification occurs only in time

Key Takeaway
The divine will has only two attachments, and all agency belongs solely to Allah's Essence — attributing actions to attributes is merely metaphorical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something in life, do you genuinely believe that the 'real cause' is the Most Holy Essence, or do you feel as though your skills or willpower were the true agents? What would it look like to live in radical reliance on Allah alone, attributing every success and failure directly to Him?
?
If the act of attributing effect to power is a mental metaphor, then what is the reality of your own power? How does this shift your understanding of personal responsibility and dependence on Allah?
?
This lesson argues that even the will's specification is metaphorically attributed to the will. Does that confront you with the fact that every 'decision' you think you make is ultimately from Allah? How can you cultivate a heart that sees the Hand of Allah behind every ‘cause’ and yet does not neglect the means?
